# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Document Cilium eBPF Map API

## Objective

Generate comprehensive API reference documentation for Cilium's eBPF map API in the `pkg/bpf` package. The documentation should serve as a complete reference for developers working with eBPF maps in Cilium.

## Scope

Focus on the Go wrappers in `pkg/bpf` that provide user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. Document:

1. **Core Map Type and Creation**
   - `Map` struct and its primary methods
   - Map creation functions (`NewMap`, `OpenMap`, `OpenOrCreate`)
   - Map lifecycle operations (Open, Create, Close, Recreate)

2. **CRUD Operations**
   - Lookup, Update, Delete operations
   - Batch operations (BatchLookup, DeleteAll)
   - Per-CPU map operations
   - Locked operations (DeleteLocked)

3. **Iteration and Dumping**
   - Dump methods and callbacks
   - BatchIterator type and usage
   - DumpStats for tracking iteration

4. **Pinning and Persistence**
   - Pin/Unpin operations
   - BPF filesystem paths (BPFFSRoot, CiliumPath, MapPath)
   - Map persistence behavior

5. **Key/Value Interfaces**
   - MapKey, MapValue, MapPerCPUValue interfaces
   - EndpointKey as concrete example

6. **Event System**
   - Event types (MapUpdate, MapDelete)
   - DumpAndSubscribe for event streaming
   - Event callbacks and handles

7. **Collection Loading**
   - LoadCollection and LoadAndAssign functions
   - CollectionOptions

## Requirements

Your documentation must include:

1. **API Method Signatures**: Complete signatures with parameter types and return values
2. **Behavioral Semantics**:
   - When maps are pinned vs unpinned
   - Difference between Create() and CreateUnpinned()
   - OpenOrCreate() behavior on existing maps
   - How deletion works within DumpCallback (requires DeleteLocked)
   - Event subscription lifecycle
   - Batch iterator retry behavior on ENOSPC
3. **Usage Examples**: Code snippets showing:
   - Basic map creation and CRUD
   - Iteration with BatchIterator
   - Event subscription and cleanup
   - Pinning and unpinning maps
   - Real-world patterns from Cilium internals
4. **Documentation Structure**: Organize clearly with sections for each category above

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format.

## Constraints

- Do NOT include file paths or specific implementation locations in the documentation
- Focus on API contracts and behavior, not internal implementation details
- Include enough behavioral detail that users can correctly use the API without reading source code
- Provide accurate examples that would compile and work correctly

The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what was documented:

**Structure (12 sections):**

1. **Key/Value Interfaces** — `MapKey`, `MapValue`, `MapPerCPUValue` with method requirements and the `EndpointKey` concrete example.

2. **Core Map Type** — The `Map` struct, its behavioral properties, builder methods (`WithCache`, `WithEvents`, `WithPressureMetric`, etc.), and all property accessors.

3. **Map Creation Functions** — `NewMap`, `NewMapWithInnerSpec`, `OpenMap` with full signatures and examples.

4. **Map Lifecycle Operations** — `OpenOrCreate`, `Create`, `CreateUnpinned`, `Open`, `Recreate`, `Close`, `IsOpen` with detailed behavioral semantics for each (especially pinning vs. not pinning).

5. **CRUD Operations** — `Lookup`, `Update`, `Delete`, `SilentDelete`, `DeleteLocked` (with the critical note that it must be called from inside a `DumpCallback`), `DeleteAll`, `ClearAll`.

6. **Iteration and Dumping** — `DumpCallback`, `DumpWithCallback`, `DumpReliablyWithCallback` (with lock behavior and ErrMaxLookup guard), `DumpPerCPUWithCallback`, `Dump`, `DumpStats` field-by-field.

7. **Batch Operations** — `BatchLookup`, `BatchCount`, `BatchIterator` generics, `IterateAll`, ENOSPC retry behavior, all iterator options, `CountAll`.

8. **Pinning and Persistence** — All filesystem path functions, `CheckOrMountFS`, `MkdirBPF`, `Unpin`, `UnpinIfExists` with semantics table.

9. **Event System** — Action constants, `Event` accessors, `EventCallbackFunc`, `DumpAndSubscribe`, `Handle.C()` back-pressure behavior and forced close semantics.

10. **Collection Loading** — `LoadCollectionSpec` (tail call reachability analysis), `LoadCollection` (commit function semantics), `LoadAndAssign`, `CollectionOptions`.

11. **StateDB Reconci

It is identical to Open() but should be used when\\n643: // m.lock is already held. open() may only be used if m.lock is held for\\n644: // writing.\\n645: func (m *Map) open() error {\\n646: \\tif m.m != nil {\\n647: \\t\\treturn nil\\n648: \\t}\\n649: \\n650: \\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\\n651: \\t\\treturn err\\n652: \\t}\\n653: \\n654: \\tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(m.path, nil)\\n655: \\tif err != nil {\\n656: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"loading pinned map %s: %w\\\", m.path, err)\\n657: \\t}\\n658: \\n659: \\tm.updateMetrics()\\n660: \\tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\\n661: \\n662: \\tm.m = em\\n663: \\n664: \\treturn nil\\n665: }\\n666: \\n667: func (m *Map) Close() error {\\n668: \\tm.lock.Lock()\\n669: \\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\\n670: \\n671: \\tif m.enableSync {\\n672: \\t\\tmapControllers.RemoveController(m.controllerName())\\n673: \\t}\\n674: \\n675: \\tif m.m != nil {\\n676: \\t\\tm.m.Close()\\n677: \\t\\tm.m = nil\\n678: \\t}\\n679: \\n680: \\tunregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\\n681: \\n682: \\treturn nil\\n683: }\\n684: \\n685: func (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error {\\n686: \\tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\\n687: \\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\\n688: \\t\\tduration = spanstat.Start()\\n689: \\t}\\n690: \\n691: \\terr := m.m.NextKey(key, nextKeyOut)\\n692: \\n693: \\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\\n694: \\t\\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpGetNextKey, metrics.Error2Outcome(err)).Observe(duration.End(err == nil).Total().Seconds())\\n695: \\t}\\n696: \\n697: \\treturn err\\n698: }\\n699: \\n700: type DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\\n701: \\n702: // DumpWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given DumpCallback for\\n703: // each map entry. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n705: //\\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n708: \\tif cb == nil {\\n709: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n710: \\t}\\n711: \\n712: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n713: \\t\\treturn err\\n714: \\t}\\n715: \\n716: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n717: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n718: \\n719: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n720: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n721: \\tmv := m.value.New()\\n722: \\n723: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n724: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n725: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n726: \\n727: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n728: \\t\\tmv = m.value.New()\\n729: \\t}\\n730: \\n731: \\treturn i.Err()\\n732: }\\n733: \\n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\\n737: \\n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\\n743: \\tif cb == nil {\\n744: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n745: \\t}\\n746: \\n747: \\tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\\n748: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\\\", m.name)\\n749: \\t}\\n750: \\n751: \\tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\\n752: \\tif !ok {\\n753: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\\\", m.name)\\n754: \\t}\\n755: \\n756: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n757: \\t\\treturn err\\n758: \\t}\\n759: \\n760: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n761: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n762: \\n763: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n764: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n765: \\tmv := v.NewSlice()\\n766: \\n767: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n768: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n769: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n770: \\n771: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n772: \\t\\tmv = v.NewSlice()\\n773: \\t}\\n774: \\n775: \\treturn i.Err()\\n776: }\\n777: \\n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n781: \\tfound, err := m.exist()\\n782: \\tif err != nil {\\n783: \\t\\treturn err\\n784: \\t}\\n785: \\n786: \\tif found {\\n787: \\t\\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\\n788: \\t}\\n789: \\n790: \\treturn nil\\n791: }\\n792: \\n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\\n799: //\\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\\n804: \\tif cb == nil {\\n805: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n806: \\t}\\n807: \\n808: \\tif stats == nil {\\n809: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"stats is nil\\\")\\n810: \\t}\\n811: \\n812: \\tvar (\\n813: \\t\\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\\n814: \\t\\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\\n815: \\t\\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\\n816: \\t\\tvalue      = m.value.New()\\n817: \\n818: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n819: \\t)\\n820: \\n821: \\tstats.start()\\n822: \\tdefer stats.finish()\\n823: \\n824: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n825: \\t\\treturn err\\n826: \\t}\\n827: \\n828: \\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\\n829: \\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\\n830: \\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\\n831: \\tm.lock.Lock()\\n832: \\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\\n833: \\tif m.m == nil {\\n834: \\t\\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\\n835: \\t\\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\\n836: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"map is closed\\\")\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\n839: \\t// Get the first map key.\\n840: \\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\\n841: \\t\\tstats.Lookup = 1\\n842: \\t\\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n843: \\t\\t\\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\\n844: \\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n845: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n846: \\t\\t}\\n847: \\t}\\n848: \\n849: \\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\\n850: \\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\\n851: \\t// updated while being iterated)\\n852: \\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\\n853: \\n854: \\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\\n855: \\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\\n856: \\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\\n857: \\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\\n858: \\t\\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\\n859: \\t\\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\\n860: \\t\\t//\\n861: \\t\\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\\n862: \\t\\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\\n863: \\t\\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\\n864: \\t\\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\\n865: \\t\\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\\n866: \\n867: \\t\\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\\n868: \\t\\t\\tstats.LookupFailed++\\n869: \\t\\t\\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\\n870: \\t\\t\\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\\n871: \\t\\t\\tif prevKeyValid {\\n872: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = prevKey\\n873: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\\n874: \\t\\t\\t\\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\\n875: \\t\\t\\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n876: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.KeyFallback++\\n877: \\t\\t\\t} else {\\n878: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\\n879: \\t\\t\\t\\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\\n880: \\t\\t\\t\\t// one, or the first element in the map.\\n881: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n882: \\t\\t\\t\\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\\n883: \\t\\t\\t\\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\\n884: \\t\\t\\t\\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\\n885: \\t\\t\\t\\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n887: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Interrupted++\\n888: \\t\\t\\t}\\n889: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n890: \\t\\t}\\n891: \\n892: \\t\\tcb(currentKey, value)\\n893: \\n894: \\t\\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\\n895: \\t\\t\\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n896: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n897: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\\n898: \\t\\t\\t}\\n899: \\t\\t\\treturn nextKeyErr\\n900: \\t\\t}\\n901: \\n902: \\t\\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\\n903: \\t\\tprevKey = currentKey\\n904: \\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n905: \\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n906: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = true\\n907: \\t}\\n908: \\n909: \\treturn ErrMaxLookup\\n910: }\\n911: \\n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\\n913: // of bpf maps.\\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\\n915: \\tm    *Map\\n916: \\terr  error\\n917: \\tkeys []KT\\n918: \\tvals []VT\\n919: \\n920: \\tchunkSize      int\\n921: \\tmaxDumpRetries uint32\\n922: \\n923: \\t// Iteration stats\\n924: \\tbatchSize int\\n925: \\n926: \\topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\\n927: }\\n928: \\n929: // NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\\n930: // This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\\n951: //\\t\\t// ...\\n952: //\\t}\\n953: func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, \\treturn kvs.err\\n979: }\\n980: \\n981: func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\\n982: \\tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\\n983: \\t\\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\\n984: \\t}\\n985: \\treturn defaultBatchedRetries\\n986: }\\n987: \\n988: const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\\n989: \\n990: type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\\n991: \\n992: // WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\\n993: // BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1011: \\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1012: \\t\\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\\n1013: \\t\\treturn in\\n1014: \\t}\\n1015: }\\n1016: \\n1017: // WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\\n1018: // chosen starting chunk size.\\n1019: func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1020: \\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1021: \\t\\tin.chunkSize = size\\n1022: \\t\\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\\n1023: \\t\\t\\tin.chunkSize = 8\\n1024: \\t\\t}\\n1025: \\t\\treturn in\\n1026: \\t}\\n1027: }\\n1028: \\n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\\n1030: // iterator.\\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\\n1032: \\tc := 0\\n1033: \\tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\\n1034: \\t\\tc++\\n1035: \\t}\\n1036: \\treturn c, iter.Err()\\n1037: }\\n1038: \\n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\\n1040: \\tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\\n1041: \\tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\\n1042: \\treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\\n1043: }\\n1044: \\n1045: // IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\\n1046: // using the batched API.\\n1047: // In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\\n1048: // this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\\n1049: // of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\\n1050: // If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\\n1051: // will be returned via Err().\\n1052: //\\n1053: // All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\\n1054: //\\n1055: // If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\\n1056: func (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\\n1057: \\tswitch bi.m.Type() {\\n1058: \\tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\\n1059: \\t\\tbreak\\n1060: \\tdefault:\\n1061: \\t\\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\\\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\\\", bi.m.Type())\\n1062: \\t\\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\\n1063: \\t}\\n1064: \\n1065: \\tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\\n1066: \\n1067: \\tfor _, opt := range opts {\\n1068: \\t\\tif opt != nil {\\n1069: \\t\\t\\tbi = opt(bi)\\n1070: \\t\\t}\\n1071: \\t}\\n1072: \\n1073: \\t// reset values\\n1074: \\tbi.err = nil\\n1075: \\tbi.batchSize = 0\\n1076: \\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1077: \\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1078: \\n1079: \\tprocessed := 0\\n1080: \\tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\\n1081: \\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {\\n1082: \\t\\tif bi.Err() != nil {\\n1083: \\t\\t\\treturn\\n1084: \\t\\t}\\n1085: \\n1086: \\titerate:\\n1087: \\t\\tfor {\\n1088: \\t\\t\\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\\n1089: \\t\\t\\t\\tbi.err = ctx.Err()\\n1090: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n1091: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1092: \\t\\tretry:\\n1093: \\t\\t\\tfor retry := range bi.maxBatchedRetries() {\\n1094: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\\n1095: \\t\\t\\t\\tc, batchErr := bi.m.BatchLookup(&cursor, bi.keys, bi.vals, nil)\\n1096: \\t\\t\\t\\tbi.batchSize = c\\n1097: \\n1098: \\t\\t\\t\\tdone := errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\\n1099: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\\n1100: \\t\\t\\t\\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\\n1101: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\\n1102: \\t\\t\\t\\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\\n1103: \\t\\t\\t\\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\\n1104: \\t\\t\\t\\t//\\n1105: \\t\\t\\t\\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to recover by growing the batch buffer\\n1106: \\t\\t\\t\\t// size (up to some max number of retries - default: 3) and retrying the iteration.\\n1107: \\t\\t\\t\\t//\\n1108: \\t\\t\\t\\t// [1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.12.6/source/kernel/bpf/hashtab.c#L1807-L1809\\n1109: \\t\\t\\t\\t//\\n1110: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Note: If this failure happens during the bpf syscall, it is expected that the underlying\\n1111: \\t\\t\\t\\t// cursor will not have been swapped - meaning that we can retry the iteration at the same cursor.\\n1112: \\t\\t\\t\\tif errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC) {\\n1113: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tif retry == bi.maxBatchedRetries()-1 {\\n1114: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.err = batchErr\\n1115: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t} else {\\n1116: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.chunkSize *= 2\\n1117: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1118: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1119: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1120: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue retry\\n1121: \\t\\t\\t\\t} \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\\\"failed to iterate map: %w\\\", batchErr)\\n1125: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n1126: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1127: \\n1128: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Yield all received pairs.\\n1129: \\t\\t\\t\\tfor i := range bi.batchSize {\\n1130: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tprocessed++\\n1131: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tif !yield(&bi.keys[i], &bi.vals[i]) {\\n1132: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbreak iterate\\n1133: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1134: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1135: \\n1136: \\t\\t\\t\\tif done {\\n1137: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbreak iterate\\n1138: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1139: \\t\\t\\t\\tbreak retry // finish retry loop for this batch.\\n1140: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1141: \\t\\t}\\n1142: \\t}\\n1143: }\\n1144: \\n1145: // Dump returns the map (type map[string][]string) which contains all\\n1146: // data stored in BPF map.\\n1147: func It is identical to Open() but should be used when\n643: // m.lock is already held. open() may only be used if m.lock is held for\n644: // writing.\n645: func (m *Map) open() error {\n646: \tif m.m != nil {\n647: \t\treturn nil\n648: \t}\n649: \n650: \tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n651: \t\treturn err\n652: \t}\n653: \n654: \tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(m.path, nil)\n655: \tif err != nil {\n656: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"loading pinned map %s: %w\", m.path, err)\n657: \t}\n658: \n659: \tm.updateMetrics()\n660: \tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n661: \n662: \tm.m = em\n663: \n664: \treturn nil\n665: }\n666: \n667: func (m *Map) Close() error {\n668: \tm.lock.Lock()\n669: \tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n670: \n671: \tif m.enableSync {\n672: \t\tmapControllers.RemoveController(m.controllerName())\n673: \t}\n674: \n675: \tif m.m != nil {\n676: \t\tm.m.Close()\n677: \t\tm.m = nil\n678: \t}\n679: \n680: \tunregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n681: \n682: \treturn nil\n683: }\n684: \n685: func (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error {\n686: \tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\n687: \tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n688: \t\tduration = spanstat.Start()\n689: \t}\n690: \n691: \terr := m.m.NextKey(key, nextKeyOut)\n692: \n693: \tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n694: \t\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpGetNextKey, metrics.Error2Outcome(err)).Observe(duration.End(err == nil).Total().Seconds())\n695: \t}\n696: \n697: \treturn err\n698: }\n699: \n700: type DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n701: \n702: // DumpWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given DumpCallback for\n703: // each map entry. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n705: //\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\n708: \tif cb == nil {\n709: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n710: \t}\n711: \n712: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n713: \t\treturn err\n714: \t}\n715: \n716: \tm.lock.RLock()\n717: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n718: \n719: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n720: \tmk := m.key.New()\n721: \tmv := m.value.New()\n722: \n723: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n724: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n725: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n726: \n727: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n728: \t\tmv = m.value.New()\n729: \t}\n730: \n731: \treturn i.Err()\n732: }\n733: \n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n737: \n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\n743: \tif cb == nil {\n744: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n745: \t}\n746: \n747: \tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\n748: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\", m.name)\n749: \t}\n750: \n751: \tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\n752: \tif !ok {\n753: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\", m.name)\n754: \t}\n755: \n756: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n757: \t\treturn err\n758: \t}\n759: \n760: \tm.lock.RLock()\n761: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n762: \n763: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n764: \tmk := m.key.New()\n765: \tmv := v.NewSlice()\n766: \n767: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n768: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n769: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n770: \n771: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n772: \t\tmv = v.NewSlice()\n773: \t}\n774: \n775: \treturn i.Err()\n776: }\n777: \n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\n781: \tfound, err := m.exist()\n782: \tif err != nil {\n783: \t\treturn err\n784: \t}\n785: \n786: \tif found {\n787: \t\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \treturn nil\n791: }\n792: \n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n799: //\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n804: \tif cb == nil {\n805: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n806: \t}\n807: \n808: \tif stats == nil {\n809: \t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n810: \t}\n811: \n812: \tvar (\n813: \t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n814: \t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n815: \t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n816: \t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n817: \n818: \t\tprevKeyValid = false\n819: \t)\n820: \n821: \tstats.start()\n822: \tdefer stats.finish()\n823: \n824: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n825: \t\treturn err\n826: \t}\n827: \n828: \t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n829: \t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n830: \t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n831: \tm.lock.Lock()\n832: \tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n833: \tif m.m == nil {\n834: \t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n835: \t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n836: \t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n837: \t}\n838: \n839: \t// Get the first map key.\n840: \tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n841: \t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n842: \t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n843: \t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n844: \t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n845: \t\t\treturn nil\n846: \t\t}\n847: \t}\n848: \n849: \t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n850: \t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n851: \t// updated while being iterated)\n852: \tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n853: \n854: \t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n855: \t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n856: \t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n857: \tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n858: \t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\n859: \t\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\n860: \t\t//\n861: \t\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\n862: \t\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\n863: \t\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\n864: \t\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\n865: \t\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\n866: \n867: \t\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\n868: \t\t\tstats.LookupFailed++\n869: \t\t\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\n870: \t\t\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\n871: \t\t\tif prevKeyValid {\n872: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = prevKey\n873: \t\t\t\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\n874: \t\t\t\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\n875: \t\t\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n876: \t\t\t\tstats.KeyFallback++\n877: \t\t\t} else {\n878: \t\t\t\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\n879: \t\t\t\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\n880: \t\t\t\t// one, or the first element in the map.\n881: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n882: \t\t\t\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\n883: \t\t\t\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\n884: \t\t\t\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\n885: \t\t\t\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\n886: \t\t\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n887: \t\t\t\tstats.Interrupted++\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t\tcontinue\n890: \t\t}\n891: \n892: \t\tcb(currentKey, value)\n893: \n894: \t\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\n895: \t\t\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n896: \t\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n897: \t\t\t\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\n898: \t\t\t}\n899: \t\t\treturn nextKeyErr\n900: \t\t}\n901: \n902: \t\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\n903: \t\tprevKey = currentKey\n904: \t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n905: \t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n906: \t\tprevKeyValid = true\n907: \t}\n908: \n909: \treturn ErrMaxLookup\n910: }\n911: \n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\n913: // of bpf maps.\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n915: \tm    *Map\n916: \terr  error\n917: \tkeys []KT\n918: \tvals []VT\n919: \n920: \tchunkSize      int\n921: \tmaxDumpRetries uint32\n922: \n923: \t// Iteration stats\n924: \tbatchSize int\n925: \n926: \topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\n927: }\n928: \n929: // NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n930: // This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n931: // when end of map is reached.\n932: // Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n933: // the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n934: // The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\n935: //\n936: // Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\n937: // iteration over.\n938: //\n939: // Example usage:\n940: //\n941: //\tm := NewMap(\"cilium_test\",\n942: //\t\tebpf.Hash,\n943: //\t\t&TestKey{}, \t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\n944: //\t\t&TestValue{}, \t// *TestValue implements MapValue.\n945: //\t\tmapSize,\n946: //\t\tBPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n947: //\t)\n948: //\n949: //\titer := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n950: //\tfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n951: //\t\t// ...\n952: //\t}\n953: func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n954: \treturn &BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]{\n955: \t\tm: m,\n956: \t}\n957: }\n958: \n959: // KeyPointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n960: // of a type T is a MapKey.\n961: type KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n962: \tMapKey\n963: \t*T\n964: }\n965: \n966: // ValuePointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n967: // of a type T is a MapValue.\n968: type ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n969: \tMapValue\n970: \t*T\n971: }\n972: \n973: // Err returns errors encountered during the previous iteration when\n974: // IterateAll(...) is called.\n975: //\n976: // If the iterator is reused, the error will be reset,\n977: func (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error {\n978: \treturn kvs.err\n979: }\n980: \n981: func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\n982: \tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\n983: \t\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\n984: \t}\n985: \treturn defaultBatchedRetries\n986: }\n987: \n988: const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\n989: \n990: type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n991: \n992: // WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\n993: // BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH options.\n994: func WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n995: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n996: \t\tin.opts = opts\n997: \t\treturn in\n998: \t}\n999: }\n1000: \n1001: // WithMaxRetries returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the default\n1002: // max batch retries.\n1003: //\n1004: // Unless the starting chunk size is set to be the map size, it is possible for iteration\n1005: // to fail with ENOSPC if the passed allocated chunk array size is not big enough to accommodate\n1006: // a the bpf maps underlying hashmaps bucket size.\n1007: //\n1008: // If this happens, BatchIterator will automatically attempt to double the batch size and\n1009: // retry the iteration from the same place - up to a number of retries.\n1010: func WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1011: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1012: \t\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\n1013: \t\treturn in\n1014: \t}\n1015: }\n1016: \n1017: // WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\n1018: // chosen starting chunk size.\n1019: func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1020: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1021: \t\tin.chunkSize = size\n1022: \t\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\n1023: \t\t\tin.chunkSize = 8\n1024: \t\t}\n1025: \t\treturn in\n1026: \t}\n1027: }\n1028: \n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\n1030: // iterator.\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\n1032: \tc := 0\n1033: \tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n1034: \t\tc++\n1035: \t}\n1036: \treturn c, iter.Err()\n1037: }\n1038: \n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\n1040: \tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\n1041: \tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\n1042: \treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\n1043: }\n1044: \n1045: // IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\n1046: // using the batched API.\n1047: // In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\n1048: // this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\n1049: // of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\n1050: // If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\n1051: // will be returned via Err().\n1052: //\n1053: // All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\n1054: //\n1055: // If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\n1056: func (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\n1057: \tswitch bi.m.Type() {\n1058: \tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\n1059: \t\tbreak\n1060: \tdefault:\n1061: \t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\", bi.m.Type())\n1062: \t\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\n1063: \t}\n1064: \n1065: \tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\n1066: \n1067: \tfor _, opt := range opts {\n1068: \t\tif opt != nil {\n1069: \t\t\tbi = opt(bi)\n1070: \t\t}\n1071: \t}\n1072: \n1073: \t// reset values\n1074: \tbi.err = nil\n1075: \tbi.batchSize = 0\n1076: \tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n1077: \tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n1078: \n1079: \tprocessed := 0\n1080: \tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\n1081: \treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {\n1082: \t\tif bi.Err() != nil {\n1083: \t\t\treturn\n1084: \t\t}\n1085: \n1086: \titerate:\n1087: \t\tfor {\n1088: \t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n1089: \t\t\t\tbi.err = ctx.Err()\n1090: \t\t\t\treturn\n1091: \t\t\t}\n1092: \t\tretry:\n1093: \t\t\tfor retry := range bi.maxBatchedRetries() {\n1094: \t\t\t\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\n1095: \t\t\t\tc, batchErr := bi.m.BatchLookup(&cursor, bi.keys, bi.vals, nil)\n1096: \t\t\t\tbi.batchSize = c\n1097: \n1098: \t\t\t\tdone := errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\n1099: \t\t\t\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\n1100: \t\t\t\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\n1101: \t\t\t\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\n1102: \t\t\t\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\n1103: \t\t\t\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\n1104: \t\t\t\t//\n1105: \t\t\t\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to recover by growing the batch buffer\n1106: \t\t\t\t// size (up to some max number of retries - default: 3) and retrying the iteration.\n1107: \t\t\t\t//\n1108: \t\t\t\t// [1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.12.6/source/kernel/bpf/hashtab.c#L1807-L1809\n1109: \t\t\t\t//\n1110: \t\t\t\t// Note: If this failure happens during the bpf syscall, it is expected that the underlying\n1111: \t\t\t\t// cursor will not have been swapped - meaning that we can retry the iteration at the same cursor.\n1112: \t\t\t\tif errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC) {\n1113: \t\t\t\t\tif retry == bi.maxBatchedRetries()-1 {\n1114: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.err = batchErr\n1115: \t\t\t\t\t} else {\n1116: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.chunkSize *= 2\n1117: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n1118: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n1119: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1120: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue retry\n1121: \t\t\t\t} else if !done && batchErr != nil {\n1122: \t\t\t\t\t// If we're not done, and we didn't hit a ENOSPC then stop iteration and record\n1123: \t\t\t\t\t// the error.\n1124: \t\t\t\t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"failed to iterate map: %w\", batchErr)\n1125: \t\t\t\t\treturn\n1126: \t\t\t\t}\n1127: \n1128: \t\t\t\t// Yield all received pairs.\n1129: \t\t\t\tfor i := range bi.batchSize {\n1130: \t\t\t\t\tprocessed++\n1131: \t\t\t\t\tif !yield(&bi.keys[i], &bi.vals[i]) {\n1132: \t\t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n1133: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1134: \t\t\t\t}\n1135: \n1136: \t\t\t\tif done {\n1137: \t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n1138: \t\t\t\t}\n1139: \t\t\t\tbreak retry // finish retry loop for this batch.\n1140: \t\t\t}\n1141: \t\t}\n1142: \t}\n1143: }\n1144: \n1145: // Dump returns the map (type map[string][]string) which contains all\n1146: // data stored in BPF map.\n1147: func (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error {\n1148: \tcallback := func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n1149: \t\t// No need to deep copy since we are creating strings.\n1150: \t\thash[key.String()] = append(hash[key.String()], value.String())\n1151: \t}\n1152: \n1153: \tif err := m.DumpWithCallback(callback); err != nil {\n1154: \t\treturn err\n1155: inline ASM this generates the following instructions:\n178: \t\t\t//   Mov R1, Rx\n179: \t\t\t//   Mov R2, <map>\n180: \t\t\t//   Mov R3, <index>\n181: \t\t\t//   call tail_call\n182: \n183: \t\t\t// Any pinned maps incompatible with the given spec are\n106: // removed and recreated.\n107: //\n108: // If spec.Pinned is 0, a new Map is always created.\n109: func OpenOrCreateMap(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.MapSpec, pinDir string) (*ebpf.Map, error) {\n110: \tvar opts ebpf.MapOptions\n111: \tif spec.Pinning != 0 {\n112: \t\tif pinDir == \"\" {\n113: \t\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"cannot pin map to empty pinDir\")\n114: \t\t}\n115: \t\tif spec.Name == \"\" {\n116: \t\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"cannot load unnamed map from pin\")\n117: \t\t}\n118: \n119: \t\tif err := MkdirBPF(pinDir); err != nil {\n120: \t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"creating map base pinning directory: %w\", err)\n121: \t\t}\n122: \n123: \t\topts.PinPath = pinDir\n124: \t}\n125: \n126: \tm, err := createMap(spec, &opts)\n127: \tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible) {\n128: \t\t// Found incompatible map. Open the pin again to find out why.\n129: \t\tm, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(path.Join(pinDir, spec.Name), nil)\n130: \t\tif err != nil {\n131: \t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"open pin of incompatible map: %w\", err)\n132: \t\t}\n133: \t\tdefer m.Close()\n134: \n135: \t\tlogger.Info(\n136: \t\t\t\"Unpinning map with incompatible properties\",\n137: \t\t\tlogfields.Path, path.Join(pinDir, spec.Name),\n138: \t\t\tlogfields.Old, []any{\n139: \t\t\t\tlogfields.Type, m.Type(),\n140: \t\t\t\tlogfields.KeySize, m.KeySize(),\n141: \t\t\t\tlogfields.ValueSize, m.ValueSize(),\n142: \t\t\t\tlogfields.MaxEntries, m.MaxEntries(),\n143: \t\t\t\tlogfields.Flags, m.Flags(),\n144: \t\t\t},\n145: \t\t\tlogfields.New, []any{\n146: \t\t\t\tlogfields.Type, spec.Type,\n147: \t\t\t\tlogfields.KeySize, spec.KeySize,\n148: \t\t\t\tlogfields.ValueSize, spec.ValueSize,\n149: \t\t\t\tlogfields.MaxEntries, spec.MaxEntries,\n150: \t\t\t\tlogfields.Flags, spec.Flags,\n151: \t\t\t},\n152: \t\t)\n153: \n154: \t\t// Existing map incompatible with spec.
