  "content": "# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\nThis document provides a comprehensive reference for the Go user-space API in the `pkg/bpf` package that wraps kernel eBPF maps. It covers map creation, CRUD operations, iteration, pinning, events, and collection loading.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n2. [Core Map Type](#core-map-type)\n3. [Map Creation Functions](#map-creation-functions)\n4. [Map Lifecycle Operations](#map-lifecycle-operations)\n5. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n6. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n7. [Batch Operations](#batch-operations)\n8. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n9. [Event System](#event-system)\n10. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n11. [StateDB Reconciler Integration](#statedb-reconciler-integration)\n12. [Helper Utilities](#helper-utilities)\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\nAll keys and values stored in a `Map` must satisfy one of the following interfaces.\n\n### `MapKey`\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n`MapKey` is the interface every BPF map key type must implement.\n\n- `String() string` \u2014 returns a human-readable representation of the key, used in logging and as the in-memory cache key string.\n- `New() MapKey` \u2014 allocates and returns a fresh, zeroed pointer to a new instance of the same concrete type. Called internally during iteration to avoid reuse of the same buffer.\n\n### `MapValue`\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n`MapValue` is the interface every BPF map value type must implement.\n\n- `String() string` \u2014 returns a human-readable representation of the value.\n- `New() MapValue` \u2014 allocates and returns a fresh, zeroed pointer to a new instance of the same concrete type.\n\n### `MapPerCPUValue`\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n`MapPerCPUValue` extends `MapValue` for maps of type `PerCPUHash`, `PerCPUArray`, `LRUCPUHash`, or `PerCPUCGroupStorage`. Implement this interface to enable per-CPU value iteration via `DumpPerCPUWithCallback`.\n\n- `NewSlice() any` \u2014 allocates and returns a pointer to a slice whose element type is the concrete value struct. The slice is sized to the number of online CPUs.\n\n### Concrete Example: `EndpointKey`\n\n`EndpointKey` is a concrete example of a `MapKey` used in Cilium's endpoint BPF maps. It encodes both IPv4 and IPv6 addresses as a union in the lowest bytes of a 16-byte field.\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6 // holds both IPv6 and IPv4 (in the lowest 4 bytes)\n    Family    uint8      // EndpointKeyIPv4 (1) or EndpointKeyIPv6 (2)\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n\nfunc NewEndpointKey(ip net.IP, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey\nfunc (k EndpointKey) ToIP() net.IP\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string\n```\n\n**Usage:**\n\n```go\nkey := bpf.NewEndpointKey(net.ParseIP(\"10.0.0.1\"), 0)\nfmt.Println(key.String()) // \"10.0.0.1:0\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Type\n\n### `Map` Struct\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // unexported fields\n}\n```\n\n`Map` is the central type wrapping a kernel eBPF map. It is safe for concurrent use; all exported methods acquire the internal `RWMutex` appropriately.\n\nA `Map` begins life either as a blueprint (holding a `MapSpec`) or as an open handle to an existing kernel map. Once opened or created, the `MapSpec` is consumed and the live kernel handle is retained.\n\n**Key behavioral properties:**\n\n- A `Map` is not open until one of `Open()`, `OpenOrCreate()`, `CreateUnpinned()`, or `Create()` is called (or implicitly by `Lookup`/`Update`/`Delete`/`Dump*`).\n- All CRUD methods that acquire the map implicitly call `Open()` if the map is not yet open.\n- The `Map` is **not** automatically pinned to the BPF filesystem unless `OpenOrCreate()` or `Create()` is used, or the spec has a non-zero `Pinning` field.\n\n**Builder methods (configure before opening):**\n\n| Method | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| `WithCache() *Map` | Enables an in-memory value cache. Entries inserted from user-space are stored locally with their desired state and last error. Enables automatic error reconciliation via a background controller. |\n| `WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map` | Enables a bounded ring-buffer event log of all map operations (update/delete/delete-all). Required before calling `DumpAndSubscribe`. |\n| `WithGroupName(group string) *Map` | Sets the metric group name for capacity/pressure metrics. |\n| `WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map` | Enables map pressure tracking (fill ratio) with threshold 0 (always reported). |\n| `WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map` | Enables map pressure tracking, only reported when pressure exceeds `threshold`. |\n\n**Property accessors (available before and after opening):**\n\n| Method | Signature | Description |\n|--------|-----------|-------------|\n| `Name` | `() string` | Returns the map's base name. |\n| `Path` | `() (string, error)` | Returns the absolute bpffs pin path, computing it from the name if not explicitly set. |\n| `Type` | `() ebpf.MapType` | Returns the map type (Hash, Array, LPMTrie, etc.). |\n| `KeySize` | `() uint32` | Returns the key size in bytes. |\n| `ValueSize` | `() uint32` | Returns the value size in bytes. |\n| `MaxEntries` | `() uint32` | Returns the maximum number of entries the map can hold. |\n| `Flags` | `() uint32` | Returns the map flags (e.g., `BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`). |\n| `FD` | `() int` | Returns the file descriptor of the open kernel map. Panics if the map is not open. |\n| `IsOpen` | `() bool` | Returns true if the map currently has an open kernel handle. |\n\n---\n\n## Map Creation Functions\n\n### `NewMap`\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(\n    name string,\n    mapType ebpf.MapType,\n    mapKey MapKey,\n    mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int,\n    flags uint32,\n) *Map\n```\n\nConstructs a new `Map` blueprint. No kernel resources are allocated until one of the lifecycle methods is called.\n\n- `name` \u2014 the map's base name; also determines the bpffs pin path (under `tc/globals/` for the Cilium agent).\n- `mapKey` / `mapValue` \u2014 prototype instances whose concrete type determines the key/value sizes via reflection.\n- `flags` \u2014 standard BPF map creation flags (e.g., `unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`).\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntype MyKey struct {\n    Addr uint32\n}\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d\", k.Addr) }\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() bpf.MapKey { return &MyKey{} }\n\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Count uint64\n}\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d\", v.Count) }\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() bpf.MapValue { return &MyValue{} }\n\nm := bpf.NewMap(\n    \"cilium_my_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &MyKey{},\n    &MyValue{},\n    65536,\n    0,\n)\n```\n\n### `NewMapWithInnerSpec`\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(\n    name string,\n    mapType ebpf.MapType,\n    mapKey MapKey,\n    mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int,\n    flags uint32,\n    innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec,\n) *Map\n```\n\nLike `NewMap`, but also sets an inner map spec. Used for map-in-map types such as `ebpf.ArrayOfMaps` or `ebpf.HashOfMaps`.\n\n### `OpenMap`\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\nOpens an **already-pinned** BPF map from the BPF filesystem.\n\n- `pinPath` must be an absolute path.\n- The map is opened but **not** re-pinned; the pin already exists.\n- Returns the open `Map` or an error if the pin does not exist or is inaccessible.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm, err := bpf.OpenMap(\"/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/cilium_my_map\", &MyKey{}, &MyValue{})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Map Lifecycle Operations\n\n### `OpenOrCreate`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nThe primary lifecycle method for maps that should persist on the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n\n1. If the map is already open, returns `nil` immediately.\n2. Attempts to load an existing pinned map at `m.path` (which defaults to `MapPath(m.name)`).\n3. If found, validates that the existing map's type, key size, value size, max entries, and flags match the spec. If they do not match and the map is not a program array, the pin is deleted and a new map is created in its place (data loss warning: previous entries are lost).\n4. If not found, creates a new map and pins it at `m.path`.\n5. The `MapSpec` is consumed after a successful open/create, setting the internal spec field to `nil`.\n\n**Pinning:** Maps opened with `OpenOrCreate` are always pinned. The pin is created at `MapPath(m.name)` under the BPF filesystem root.\n\n### `Create`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nEquivalent to calling `OpenOrCreate()` followed immediately by `Close()`. Useful when you need the map to exist on the filesystem (e.g., to be loaded by the kernel datapath) but do not need an open file descriptor in the current process after creation.\n\n**Note:** Unlike `CreateUnpinned`, this method **does** pin the map.\n\n### `CreateUnpinned`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates the map in the kernel **without** pinning it to the BPF filesystem. The map exists only as long as there is at least one open file descriptor referencing it.\n\nUse this for transient maps used exclusively in the current process (e.g., test fixtures, ephemeral communication maps).\n\n### `Open`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens an existing pinned map by loading it from the BPF filesystem path. Does not create the map if it does not exist. Returns an error if the pin is not found.\n\nMost CRUD methods call `Open()` implicitly when the map is not yet open.\n\n### `Recreate`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves any existing pin at the map's pin path and then creates and pins a fresh map. Returns an error if the map is already open (i.e., has an open kernel handle). Use when you need a guaranteed-clean slate, discarding all previous entries.\n\n### `Close`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the kernel file descriptor. If `WithCache` was enabled, the background error resolver controller is also stopped. After `Close()`, the map can be reopened with `Open()` or `OpenOrCreate()`.\n\n### `IsOpen`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\nReturns `true` if the map currently holds an open kernel file descriptor.\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### `Lookup`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nLooks up a single entry in the map. Opens the map implicitly if not already open.\n\n- Returns the value (a newly allocated `MapValue` instance) on success.\n- Returns `nil, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if the key is not present.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\nval, err := m.Lookup(&MyKey{Addr: 0x0a000001})\nif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n    fmt.Println(\"not found\")\n} else if err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n} else {\n    fmt.Println(val.(*MyValue).Count)\n}\n```\n\n### `Update`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates an entry. Opens the map implicitly if not already open.\n\n- Semantics: `BPF_MAP_UPDATE_ELEM` with flag `BPF_ANY` (insert or update).\n- If `WithCache` is enabled, the entry is mirrored in the in-memory cache. If the kernel update fails, the cache entry is marked `Insert` (desired) with the error recorded, and a background error resolver is scheduled.\n- If `WithEvents` is enabled, a `MapUpdate` event is emitted to the event buffer.\n\n### `Delete`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes the entry for the given key. Returns an error if the key does not exist.\n\n- If `WithCache` is enabled and deletion fails, the cache entry is marked `Delete` (desired) and the background error resolver is scheduled.\n- If `WithEvents` is enabled, a `MapDelete` event is emitted.\n\n### `SilentDelete`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nDeletes the entry for the given key. If the key is not present, returns `(false, nil)` instead of an error. The `deleted` return value indicates whether the key actually existed.\n\n**Use when** missing entries are expected and you do not want spurious error metric increments.\n\n### `DeleteLocked`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes the entry for the given key, **assuming the map's internal lock is already held by the caller**.\n\n**Critical:** This method must only be called from within a `DumpCallback` (i.e., from within `DumpReliablyWithCallback`). Calling `Delete` from inside a `DumpCallback` would deadlock because the dump holds the lock for writing; `DeleteLocked` bypasses the lock acquisition, enabling safe deletion while iterating.\n\n```go\n// Correct: delete inside DumpReliablyWithCallback using DeleteLocked\nstats := bpf.NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n    if shouldDelete(key, value) {\n        _ = m.DeleteLocked(key)\n    }\n}, stats)\n```\n\n### `DeleteAll`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nDeletes all entries by iterating the map and deleting each entry individually. Opens the map implicitly if not already open.\n\n**Concurrency note:** Entries added concurrently while deletion is in progress may not be deleted (the iteration cursor may not reach them).\n\nIf `WithCache` is enabled, all cache entries are marked `Delete` prior to iteration; successfully deleted entries are removed from the cache, and failures are tracked.\n\nIf `WithEvents` is enabled, a single `MapDeleteAll` event is emitted after iteration completes.\n\n### `ClearAll`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nZeroes out the values of all entries without deleting the keys. Useful for maps where keys are fixed (e.g., per-CPU arrays). Returns an error if `WithEvents` or `WithCache` is enabled (these options are unsupported for `ClearAll`).\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### `DumpCallback`\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n```\n\nCalled once per map entry during iteration. The `key` and `value` are fresh allocations for each invocation; callers may retain them safely.\n\n**Important:** Do not call `Delete()` (or any map method that acquires the lock) from inside a `DumpCallback` used with `DumpReliablyWithCallback`. Use `DeleteLocked` instead.\n\n### `DumpWithCallback`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates all entries and invokes `cb` for each one. Not resilient to concurrent map modifications; if an entry is removed during iteration, the iterator may skip entries or restart.\n\nFor maps that may be modified during iteration, prefer `DumpReliablyWithCallback`.\n\n### `DumpWithCallbackIfExists`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback`, but returns `nil` immediately if the map's pin file does not exist, rather than returning an error.\n\n### `DumpReliablyWithCallback`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nAn iteration method that is resilient to concurrent modifications. It tracks the previously seen key so that if the current key is deleted mid-iteration, it can restart from the last valid key rather than from the beginning of the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n\n- `cb` \u2014 called for each valid entry.\n- `stats` \u2014 a `*DumpStats` initialized via `NewDumpStats(m)`; must not be nil.\n\n**Termination conditions:**\n\n- Returns `nil` when all entries have been visited (`stats.Completed == true`).\n- Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if the number of iterations exceeds `4 \u00d7 MaxEntries` (guard against infinite loops on a continuously mutated map).\n- Returns any other kernel-level error encountered.\n\n**Lock behavior:** Holds the write lock for the entire duration. This allows `DeleteLocked` to be called safely from within the callback.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nstats := bpf.NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n    k := key.(*MyKey)\n    v := value.(*MyValue)\n    fmt.Printf(\"%d -> %d\\n\", k.Addr, v.Count)\n}, stats)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"dump error: %v (lookups: %d, interrupted: %d)\", err, stats.Lookup, stats.Interrupted)\n}\n```\n\n### `DumpPerCPUWithCallback`\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates a per-CPU map and calls `cb` with the key and the full per-CPU slice of values for each entry. The value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`. The `values` argument passed to the callback is a pointer to a slice of the concrete value struct, one element per CPU.\n\n### `Dump`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nDumps the entire map into the provided `map[string][]string`, where the key is the string representation of the map key and the values are string representations of the map value(s). Suitable for simple debugging and serialization.\n\n### `DumpIfExists`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nLike `Dump`, but returns `nil` immediately if the map pin does not exist.\n\n### `DumpStats`\n\n```go\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    Started            time.Time\n    Finished           time.Time\n    Lookup             uint32\n    LookupFailed       uint32\n    PrevKeyUnavailable uint32\n    KeyFallback        uint32\n    MaxEntries         uint32\n    Interrupted        uint32\n    Completed          bool\n}\n\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\nfunc (d *DumpStats) Duration() time.Duration\n```\n\n`DumpStats` is populated by `DumpReliablyWithCallback` to track iteration quality. Fields of note:\n\n| Field | Description |\n|-------|-------------|\n| `Lookup` | Total number of `NextKey` calls performed. |\n| `LookupFailed` | Number of lookups where the key could not be found in the map (entry was deleted mid-iteration). |\n| `KeyFallback` | Number of times iteration fell back to the previous key because the current key was deleted. |\n| `Interrupted` | Number of times iteration restarted from the beginning of the map after key loss with no previous key available. |\n| `Completed` | `true` if iteration completed normally without hitting `ErrMaxLookup`. |\n\n---\n\n## Batch Operations\n\nBatch operations use the kernel's `BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH` syscall for higher throughput than single-entry lookup. They are supported only for `Hash`, `LRUHash`, and `LPMTrie` map types.\n\n### `BatchLookup`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(\n    cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor,\n    keysOut, valuesOut any,\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions,\n) (int, error)\n```\n\nPerforms a single batch lookup starting from `cursor`. Returns the number of entries read. When the map is exhausted, returns `(n, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)`.\n\n### `BatchCount`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nReturns the total number of entries in the map using repeated batch lookups. Only supported for `Hash`, `LRUHash`, and `LPMTrie` maps. Internally handles `ENOSPC` retries by doubling the chunk size.\n\n### `BatchIterator`\n\n`BatchIterator` is a typed, generic wrapper that provides ergonomic iteration via Go's range-over-function (iter.Seq2) interface.\n\n```go\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct { ... }\n\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\n**Type parameters:**\n\n- `KT` \u2014 the concrete key struct type (e.g., `MyKey`).\n- `VT` \u2014 the concrete value struct type (e.g., `MyValue`).\n- `KP` \u2014 a pointer-to-KT that also satisfies `MapKey` (e.g., `*MyKey`).\n- `VP` \u2014 a pointer-to-VT that also satisfies `MapValue` (e.g., `*MyValue`).\n\n**Important:** Each call to `IterateAll` resets all internal state, including the error. If you reuse an iterator across multiple dumps, check `Err()` before the next `IterateAll` call returns.\n\n#### `IterateAll`\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(\n    ctx context.Context,\n    opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP],\n) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\nReturns an `iter.Seq2` that yields `(*KT, *VT)` pairs. Compatible with `for k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) { ... }`.\n\n**ENOSPC retry behavior:** If the kernel returns `ENOSPC` (the allocated batch buffer was too small for the hash bucket), `BatchIterator` automatically doubles the buffer size and retries from the same cursor position. By default, up to 3 retries are attempted. If all retries are exhausted, the error is recorded in `Err()`.\n\n**Starting chunk size:** The initial buffer size is automatically computed as the nearest power of two greater than or equal to `\u221a(2 \u00d7 MaxEntries)`. This approximates the expected number of entries before the first hash collision, minimizing the likelihood of `ENOSPC`.\n\n#### `Err`\n\n```go\nfunc (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\nReturns the first error encountered during the previous call to `IterateAll`. Returns `nil` if iteration completed successfully.\n\n#### Iterator Options\n\nOptions are passed to `IterateAll` as variadic arguments:\n\n| Option Function | Description |\n|----------------|-------------|\n| `WithMaxRetries[KT, VT, KP, VP](retries uint32)` | Overrides the default 3 ENOSPC retry limit. |\n| `WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT, KP, VP](size int)` | Overrides the automatically computed starting batch buffer size. |\n| `WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT, KP, VP](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions)` | Passes low-level batch options to the underlying syscall. |\n\n#### `CountAll`\n\n```go\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    ctx context.Context,\n    iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP],\n) (int, error)\n```\n\nConvenience function that drives a `BatchIterator` to completion and returns the total entry count.\n\n**Full Example:**\n\n```go\n// MyKey implements MapKey, *MyKey implements KeyPointer[MyKey].\n// MyValue implements MapValue, *MyValue implements ValuePointer[MyValue].\n\niter := bpf.NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue, *MyKey, *MyValue](m)\n\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"key=%d value=%d\\n\", k.Addr, v.Count)\n}\n\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"iteration error: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\nBPF maps are pinned to the BPF filesystem (bpffs) to persist beyond the lifetime of the creating process. The Cilium agent mounts bpffs and uses it to share maps between the agent and the kernel datapath programs.\n\n### BPF Filesystem Paths\n\n```go\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\nfunc CiliumPath() string\nfunc TCGlobalsPath() string\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\n| Function | Returns |\n|----------|---------|\n| `BPFFSRoot()` | The root of the BPF filesystem (default: `/sys/fs/bpf`). |\n| `CiliumPath()` | `<BPFFSRoot>/cilium` \u2014 the Cilium-specific directory. |\n| `TCGlobalsPath()` | `<BPFFSRoot>/tc/globals` \u2014 the legacy map pin path used by the agent for per-node global maps. |\n| `MapPath(logger, name)` | The full path where a named map would be pinned; equivalent to `<TCGlobalsPath>/<name>` when running as the Cilium agent. |\n| `LocalMapName(name, id)` | Formats a map name with a 5-digit endpoint ID suffix: `<name><id>`. |\n| `LocalMapPath(logger, name, id)` | Equivalent to `MapPath(logger, LocalMapName(name, id))`. |\n\n**Note:** `BPFFSRoot()` and related functions lock down the root path on first access. Attempting to change the root after the first read panics.\n\n### `CheckOrMountFS`\n\n```go\nfunc CheckOrMountFS(logger *slog.Logger, bpfRoot string)\n```\n\nEnsures the BPF filesystem is mounted at `bpfRoot` (or at the default locations `/sys/fs/bpf` / `/run/cilium/bpffs` if `bpfRoot` is empty). Logs a warning and mounts automatically if not already mounted. This is called once during agent startup.\n\n### `MkdirBPF`\n\n```go\nfunc MkdirBPF(path string) error\n```\n\nCreates a directory on the BPF filesystem with the correct permissions (0755). Use this instead of `os.MkdirAll` for bpffs paths.\n\n### Pinning Methods on `Map`\n\n#### `Unpin`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n```\n\nRemoves the map's pin file from the BPF filesystem using `os.RemoveAll`. The map's kernel object remains alive as long as there is at least one open file descriptor.\n\n#### `UnpinIfExists`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\nLike `Unpin`, but does nothing and returns `nil` if the pin file does not exist.\n\n**Pin vs. unpin semantics:**\n\n- Pinning a map to bpffs keeps it alive after the pinning process exits. The kernel holds a reference as long as the pin file exists or any file descriptor is open.\n- Unpinning removes the filesystem reference, but the map continues to exist until all file descriptors are closed.\n- `OpenOrCreate` always pins. `CreateUnpinned` never pins.\n- Calling `Recreate()` removes the existing pin, then creates and re-pins a fresh map.\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\nThe event system provides an audit log of map mutations and supports live streaming of events to subscribers. It must be explicitly enabled with `WithEvents`.\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1024, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 4096,\n        TTL:     5 * time.Minute,\n    })\n```\n\n- `MaxSize` \u2014 maximum number of events held in the ring buffer. When the buffer is full, the oldest entry is overwritten.\n- `TTL` \u2014 if non-zero, a background controller runs at `TTL` intervals and evicts events older than the TTL. Set to zero to retain events indefinitely (bounded only by `MaxSize`).\n\n### Event Types\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate    Action = iota // emitted on Update()\n    MapDelete                  // emitted on Delete() / SilentDelete() / DeleteLocked()\n    MapDeleteAll               // emitted once on DeleteAll() (aggregate event)\n)\n\nfunc (e Action) String() string\n```\n\n### `Event`\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time\n    // unexported: action Action, cacheEntry (Key, Value, DesiredAction, LastError)\n}\n\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction\n```\n\n- `GetAction()` \u2014 returns `\"update\"`, `\"delete\"`, or `\"delete-all\"`.\n- `GetKey()` \u2014 returns the string representation of the key (`\"<nil>\"` for `MapDeleteAll`).\n- `GetValue()` \u2014 returns the string representation of the value (`\"<nil>\"` for deletes).\n- `GetLastError()` \u2014 returns any error from the originating operation.\n- `GetDesiredAction()` \u2014 returns the desired cache state at event time (`OK`, `Insert`, or `Delete`).\n\n### `EventCallbackFunc`\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(*Event)\n```\n\nA callback invoked once per historical event during a dump of the event buffer.\n\n### `DumpAndSubscribe`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool) (*Handle, error)\n```\n\nAtomically dumps existing events from the ring buffer and optionally establishes a live subscription. Returns a `*Handle` if `follow == true`.\n\n- `callback` \u2014 if non-nil, called synchronously for each existing event in the ring buffer (respecting the TTL filter).\n- `follow` \u2014 if `true`, returns a `*Handle` whose channel receives future events. If `false`, returns `nil, nil` after the dump.\n\nThe dump and subscription setup are performed under the map's read lock, preventing any events from being missed between the historical dump and the live subscription.\n\n**Maximum concurrent subscriptions:** 32. Attempting to exceed this limit returns an error.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nhandle, err := m.DumpAndSubscribe(func(e *bpf.Event) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"historical: %s key=%s\\n\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey())\n}, true)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer handle.Close()\n\nfor event := range handle.C() {\n    fmt.Printf(\"live: %s key=%s value=%s\\n\", event.GetAction(), event.GetKey(), event.GetValue())\n}\n\n// handle.C() is closed when Close() is called or when the subscriber falls behind.\n```\n\n### `Handle`\n\n```go\ntype Handle struct { ... }\n\nfunc (h *Handle) C() <-chan *Event\nfunc (h *Handle) Close()\n```\n\n`Handle` is the live event subscription object.\n\n- `C()` \u2014 returns a read-only channel of `*Event`. Events are buffered (channel capacity: 32). The channel is closed when `Close()` is called or when the map's event system forcibly drops the subscription.\n- `Close()` \u2014 signals that the subscriber is done. Safe to call multiple times.\n\n**Back-pressure:** The event system is non-blocking. If a subscriber's channel buffer is full when a new event arrives, the subscription is forcibly closed with an error. Subscribers must read events promptly to avoid being dropped.\n\n### `IsEventsEnabled`\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nReturns `true` if the events buffer was enabled via `WithEvents`.\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nCollection loading functions wrap `cilium/ebpf`'s collection API with Cilium-specific behaviors such as tail call resolution, map renaming, constant injection, and automatic pinning.\n\n### `CollectionOptions`\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants holds a pointer to a struct from pkg/datapath/config.\n    // Fields of the struct override BPF runtime configurables declared with DECLARE_CONFIG.\n    Constants any\n\n    // MapRenames maps CollectionSpec map keys to new names applied before loading.\n    MapRenames map[string]string\n}\n```\n\n### `LoadCollectionSpec`\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollectionSpec(logger *slog.Logger, path string) (*ebpf.CollectionSpec, error)\n```\n\nLoads and parses a BPF ELF object file into a `CollectionSpec`. In addition to standard ELF parsing, this function:\n\n1. Validates that all programs have a known type (annotated with `__section_entry` or `__declare_tail()`).\n2. Performs static reachability analysis to identify which tail call programs are reachable from the entry points.\n3. Removes unreachable tail call programs from the spec to avoid loading dead code.\n4. Populates the `cilium_calls` program array map with the reachable tail call programs.\n\n### `LoadCollection`\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(\n    logger *slog.Logger,\n    spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions,\n) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads the collection spec into the kernel. Returns:\n\n- `*ebpf.Collection` \u2014 the live collection containing all loaded programs and maps.\n- `func() error` \u2014 a **commit function** that must be called after all entry-point programs from the collection have been attached to their kernel hooks. The commit replaces map pins on the bpffs for incompatible or `CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE`-marked maps.\n- `error` \u2014 loading error, possibly a `*ebpf.VerifierError`.\n\n**The commit function is critical.** For programs sharing a tail calls map: attach all entry-points first, then call commit once. Committing too early can leave the tail calls map in an intermediate state, causing some programs to invoke stale tail call targets.\n\n**Map pinning behavior during `LoadCollection`:**\n\n- Maps with `LIBBPF_PIN_BY_NAME` in the spec are automatically loaded from `opts.Maps.PinPath/<name>` if the pin exists and is compatible.\n- If a pinned map is incompatible with the spec, the pin is removed and a fresh map is created. The new pin is committed by the returned commit function.\n- Maps marked `CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE` (`PinReplace`) are always replaced: they are created fresh and their pins are updated by the commit function.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nspec, err := bpf.LoadCollectionSpec(logger, \"/path/to/bpf_prog.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\ncoll, commit, err := bpf.LoadCollection(logger, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n    CollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n        Maps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.CiliumPath()},\n    },\n    Constants: &myDatapathConfig,\n    MapRenames: map[string]string{\"cilium_calls_00000\": \"cilium_calls_00042\"},\n})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Attach programs to hooks...\nlink, err := link.XDP(iface, coll.Programs[\"cil_xdp_entry\"], nil)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Only commit after all entry-points are attached.\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### `LoadAndAssign`\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(\n    logger *slog.Logger,\n    to any,\n    spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions,\n) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nA convenience wrapper around `LoadCollection` that additionally calls `coll.Assign(to)` to populate a struct with the collection's programs and maps. The struct fields are matched by name to the collection's programs and maps.\n\n- Returns the commit function (same semantics as `LoadCollection`).\n- On verifier error, writes the verifier log to `stderr`.\n- Wraps `LoadCollection` and `coll.Assign` errors.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nvar objs struct {\n    CilXdpEntry *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_xdp_entry\"`\n    CiliumCalls *ebpf.Map     `ebpf:\"cilium_calls\"`\n}\n\ncommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(logger, &objs, spec, opts)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer objs.CilXdpEntry.Close()\ndefer objs.CiliumCalls.Close()\n\n// Attach objs.CilXdpEntry ...\n\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## StateDB Reconciler Integration\n\nThe `pkg/bpf` package provides integration with Cilium's `statedb` reconciler for declarative BPF map management.\n\n### `KeyValue` Interface\n\n```go\ntype KeyValue interface {\n    BinaryKey() encoding.BinaryMarshaler\n    BinaryValue() encoding.BinaryMarshaler\n}\n```\n\nObjects stored in a StateDB table that are backed by a BPF map must implement `KeyValue`. The marshaled binary forms are used directly in BPF map operations.\n\n### `StructBinaryMarshaler`\n\n```go\ntype StructBinaryMarshaler struct {\n    Target any // pointer to struct\n}\n\nfunc (m StructBinaryMarshaler) MarshalBinary() ([]byte, error)\n```\n\nA convenience `BinaryMarshaler` for structs composed of primitive fields. Copies the struct's memory directly as bytes, matching the layout expected by the kernel. Use this in `BinaryKey()` and `BinaryValue()` implementations when the struct is already in the correct wire format.\n\n```go\nfunc (x *MyEntry) BinaryKey() encoding.BinaryMarshaler {\n    return bpf.StructBinaryMarshaler{&x.Key}\n}\nfunc (x *MyEntry) BinaryValue() encoding.BinaryMarshaler {\n    return bpf.StructBinaryMarshaler{&x.Value}\n}\n```\n\n### `NewMapOps`\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapOps[KV KeyValue](m *Map) reconciler.Operations[KV]\n```\n\nReturns a `reconciler.Operations[KV]` implementation backed by a `*Map`. This implements `Update`, `Delete`, and `Prune` operations suitable for use with the StateDB reconciler.\n\n- `Update` \u2014 calls `m.m.Put(kv.BinaryKey(), kv.BinaryValue())`.\n- `Delete` \u2014 calls `m.m.Delete(kv.BinaryKey())`; silently ignores missing keys.\n- `Prune` \u2014 iterates the map and deletes any entry whose key is not present in the desired state table.\n\n`ErrMapNotOpened` is returned by all operations if the map does not have an open kernel handle.\n\n---\n\n## Helper Utilities\n\n### `MapOut` (Dependency Injection)\n\n```go\ntype BpfMap any\n\ntype MapOut[T any] struct {\n    cell.Out\n    Map    T\n    BpfMap BpfMap `group:\"bpf-maps\"`\n}\n\nfunc NewMapOut[T any](m T) MapOut[T]\n```\n\n`MapOut` is a Hive/DI helper that registers a map into the `bpf-maps` value group, ensuring all maps are created before the datapath loader is invoked.\n\n**Usage in a Hive cell:**\n\n```go\ncell.Provide(func() MapOut[*MyMap] {\n    return bpf.NewMapOut(newMyMap())\n})\n```\n\n### `GetMtime`\n\n```go\nfunc GetMtime() (uint64, error)\n```\n\nReturns the current monotonic clock time in nanoseconds, matching the value returned by the `ktime_get_ns()` BPF helper. Used to compare against timeout fields in BPF map entries.\n\n### `OpenOrCreateMap` (low-level)\n\n```go\nfunc OpenOrCreateMap(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.MapSpec, pinDir string) (*ebpf.Map, error)\n```\n\nLower-level function that attempts to open a pinned map or create a new one. If the existing pin is incompatible, it is removed and the map is recreated. This underlies `Map.OpenOrCreate()` but operates directly on `ebpf.MapSpec` and `ebpf.Map`.\n\n### `LocalMapName` and `LocalMapPath`\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\nGenerate endpoint-scoped map names and paths. The `id` (endpoint ID) is zero-padded to 5 digits and appended to `name`.\n\n```go\nname := bpf.LocalMapName(\"cilium_ct4_\", 42) // \"cilium_ct4_00042\"\npath := bpf.LocalMapPath(logger, \"cilium_ct4_\", 42) // \"/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/cilium_ct4_00042\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Usage Patterns\n\n### Basic Map CRUD\n\n```go\n// 1. Define key and value types.\ntype RouteKey struct{ Prefix uint32 }\nfunc (k *RouteKey) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d\", k.Prefix) }\nfunc (k *RouteKey) New() bpf.MapKey { return &RouteKey{} }\n\ntype RouteValue struct{ NextHop uint32 }\nfunc (v *RouteValue) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d\", v.NextHop) }\nfunc (v *RouteValue) New() bpf.MapValue { return &RouteValue{} }\n\n// 2. Create and open the map.\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_routes\", ebpf.Hash, &RouteKey{}, &RouteValue{}, 1024, 0)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n\n// 3. Insert an entry.\nif err := m.Update(&RouteKey{Prefix: 0x0a000000}, &RouteValue{NextHop: 0xc0a80001}); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// 4. Look up an entry.\nval, err := m.Lookup(&RouteKey{Prefix: 0x0a000000})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"lookup: %v\", err)\n} else {\n    fmt.Printf(\"next hop: %d\\n\", val.(*RouteValue).NextHop)\n}\n\n// 5. Delete an entry.\nif err := m.Delete(&RouteKey{Prefix: 0x0a000000}); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"delete: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Iteration with `DumpReliablyWithCallback` and In-Loop Deletion\n\n```go\nstats := bpf.NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n    k := key.(*RouteKey)\n    if isStale(k) {\n        // Must use DeleteLocked inside DumpReliablyWithCallback.\n        if delErr := m.DeleteLocked(key); delErr != nil {\n            log.Printf(\"delete: %v\", delErr)\n        }\n    }\n}, stats)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"dump: %v (completed=%v)\", err, stats.Completed)\n}\n```\n\n### Batch Iteration\n\n```go\niter := bpf.NewBatchIterator[RouteKey, RouteValue, *RouteKey, *RouteValue](m)\n\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.Background()) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"%d -> %d\\n\", k.Prefix, v.NextHop)\n}\n\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"batch iteration error: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Event Subscription and Cleanup\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_routes\", ebpf.Hash, &RouteKey{}, &RouteValue{}, 1024, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 1000,\n        TTL:     10 * time.Minute,\n    })\n\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n\n// Dump historical events and subscribe to future ones.\nhandle, err := m.DumpAndSubscribe(func(e *bpf.Event) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"[historical] %s %s\\n\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey())\n}, true)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer handle.Close()\n\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\ngo func() {\n    for {\n        select {\n        case event, ok := <-handle.C():\n            if !ok {\n                // Channel closed: subscription was dropped or Close() was called.\n                return\n            }\n            fmt.Printf(\"[live] %s %s -> %s\\n\", event.GetAction(), event.GetKey(), event.GetValue())\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            return\n        }\n    }\n}()\n\n// Perform operations...\n_ = m.Update(&RouteKey{Prefix: 1}, &RouteValue{NextHop: 2})\n_ = m.Delete(&RouteKey{Prefix: 1})\n```\n\n### Pinning and Unpinning\n\n```go\n// Create and pin the map.\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_routes\", ebpf.Hash, &RouteKey{}, &RouteValue{}, 1024, 0)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\nm.Close() // Pin persists; map is accessible by path.\n\n// Later, open the map by its pin path.\nm2, err := bpf.OpenMap(bpf.MapPath(logger, \"cilium_routes\"), &RouteKey{}, &RouteValue{})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer m2.Close()\n\n// When the map is no longer needed, remove its pin.\nif err := m2.Unpin(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"unpin: %v\", err)\n}\n// m2 kernel object still alive until m2.Close() is called.\nm2.Close()\n// Now the kernel object is fully released.\n```\n",
